<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

				<strong>Abstract:</strong>
				<div class="abstract-text ng-binding" ng-bind-html="::vm.details.abstract">In this letter, a new printed dipole that uses series-connected meander open complementary split ring resonator (MOCSRR) particles is introduced. It is shown that by using the antenna presented here on a prototype passive UHF radio frequency identification (RFID) tag, useful read ranges up to 4.1 m can be achieved. The printed dipole on the prototype resonates at an overall dimension of approximately 0.1Î»<sub>0</sub>, where Î»<sub>0</sub> is the free-space wavelength at resonance. The equivalent circuit of each MOCSRR particle is extracted and compared to the equivalent circuit of an open complementary split ring resonator (OCSRR) particle with the same overall dimensions and an OCSRR particle with larger overall dimensions. It is shown that the MOCSRR particle resonates at a lower frequency than both of the OCSRR particles, thus contributing to the lower resonant frequency of the antenna. The read range of the prototype is comparable to other passive UHF RFID tags with dimensions that are up to twice the overall size.</div>
			</div><!-- end ngIf: ::vm.details.abstract -->

<div id="BodyWrapper" class="ArticlePage" xmlns:ieee="http://www.ieeexplore.ieee.org"><div id="article">
<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>Passive uhf radio frequency identification (RFID) tags typically consist of a printed antenna, a passive integrated circuit (IC) and a thin flexible substrate <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>. When designing a printed antenna for a passive UHF RFID tag, it is usually very desirable for the overall dimensions of the antenna to be as compact as possible while preserving the performance of the tag. Because of such constraints on the dimensions of the RFID tag, many novel antenna designs have been proposed <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>â<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a>. A very popular type of antenna for a RFID tag is the space-filling meander-line antenna <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a> shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a>. Each dipole arm consists of several series-connected vertical conductors (i.e., conductors in the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-1-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1" role="math" style="width: 0.544em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.483em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.48em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-3" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">y<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-1">y</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-direction) printed on a single ungrounded dielectric substrate. The current on each vertical conductor is in the opposite direction of the current on each adjacent vertical conductor. This results in a canceled far field from these elements. Thus, the radiation from the meander-line dipole is mainly due to the small horizontal segments (i.e., the segments in the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-2-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-4" role="math" style="width: 0.664em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.604em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.54em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-5"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-6" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">x</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.67em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-2">x</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-direction) connecting each vertical segment. The equivalent circuit for each meander-line section is also shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a>. The long vertical traces contribute to the capacitance of each meander-line section, while the short horizontal segments contribute to the inductance of each meander-line section. Thus, the equivalent circuit for each meander-line section is a capacitor in parallel with an inductor <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a>. It is these meander-line sections that contribute to the lower resonant frequency of the meander-line antenna.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig1"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/5423326/5608487/5608487-fig-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/5423326/5608487/5608487-fig-1-small.gif" alt="Figure 1" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 1. </b><fig><p>Meander-line antenna with the equivalent circuit elements shown in gray.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5608487/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>This letter introduces a recently developed printed dipole designed using the meander open complementary split ring resonator (MOCSRR) particle shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2(a)</a> <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a>. In particular, each pole of the dipole is formed using series-connected MOCSRR particles in the manner shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3(a)</a>. The MOCSRR particle used here is a modification of the recently published coplanar waveguide (CPW) open complementary spit ring resonator (OCSRR) particle in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a>. Instead of the concentric rings used in the OCSRR particle, the MOCSRR particle uses a meander-line path <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a>. The equivalent circuit of the MOCSRR particle is a capacitor in parallel with an inductor, which is the same equivalent circuit of the OCSRR particle. The equivalent inductance is created by the meander ring in the slot connecting port one with port two, and the equivalent capacitance is a result of the meander slots between the meander ring and the outer conducting planes. The equivalent circuit of each MOCSRR particle is the same as the equivalent circuit of each meander-line section in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a>. Therefore, by connecting the MOCSRR particles in series, the resonant frequency of a small printed dipole can be reduced in a manner similar to the meander-line antenna.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig2"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/5423326/5608487/5608487-fig-2-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/5423326/5608487/5608487-fig-2-small.gif" alt="Figure 2" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 2. </b><fig><p>(a) Meander open complementary split ring resonator particle (MOCSRR). (b) Equivalent circuit of the MOCSRR particle. (c) CPW structure used to determine the resonant frequency of the MOCSRR particle using momentum and measurements.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5608487/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>

In <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec2" class="fulltext-link">Section II</a>, the new printed dipole with series-connected MOCSRR particles is presented by designing a prototype UHF RFID tag. Next, several equivalent circuits are extracted for various MOCSRR and OCSRR particles. These equivalent circuits are then compared and discussed, and finally, conclusions are presented in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3" class="fulltext-link">Section III</a>.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>Mocsrr Uhf Rfid Tag Antenna</h2></div><p>For application purposes, the prototype RFID tag was designed to be attached to the plastic bottle cap of an empty beverage container. This required the prototype tag to be very small and still have a useful read range. The Higgs-2<a ref-type="fn" anchor="fn1" class="footnote-link"><sup>1</sup></a> by Alien Technology <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_2">[8]</a> was chosen as the passive IC on the RFID tag. At 920 MHz, the Higgs-2 IC has an input impedance of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-15-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-89" role="math" style="width: 11.114em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 9.973em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1009.91em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-90"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-91"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.505em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-92" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.841em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-93"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-94"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-95" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">I</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-96" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">C</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-97" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-98" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">13.73</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-99" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">â</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-100" style="padding-left: 0.243em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-101"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-102" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">j</span></span></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-103" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">142.8</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-104" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Â </span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-105" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î©</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-15">Z_{\rm IC}=13.73-{\rm j}142.8\ \Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_2">[8]</a>. Therefore, the antenna on the tag should have an input impedance near the conjugate of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-16-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-106" role="math" style="width: 1.685em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.505em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.5em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-107"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-108"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.505em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-109" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.841em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-110"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-111"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-112" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">I</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-113" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">C</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-16">Z_{\rm IC}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> for sufficient power delivery to the passive IC. These requirements resulted in the layout of the prototype tag with the new MOCSRR antenna shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3(b)</a>. The antenna in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3(b)</a> was designed in Momentum <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_2">[9]</a> with a 1.36-mm-thick FR-4 substrate (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-17-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-114" role="math" style="width: 3.486em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.126em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1003.07em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-115"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-116" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Îµ</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-117" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-118" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">4.2</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-17">\varepsilon=4.2</script></tex-math></inline-formula> measured and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-18-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-119" role="math" style="width: 6.369em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.709em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1005.65em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-120"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-121" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">tan</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-122"></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-123" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic; padding-left: 0.183em;">Î´<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-124" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-125" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">0.011</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-18">\tan\delta=0.011</script></tex-math></inline-formula> measured).</p><p>It should be mentioned that several design iterations lead to the antenna on the prototype tag in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3(b)</a>. There are two reasons for this. First, the modeling software, Momentum, is restricted to planar structures. The RFID tag was being applied to a three-dimensional problem that was approximated in Momentum. Second, the material properties of the plastic cap were unknown. Even with these uncertainties, a gain of 0.917 dBi and an input impedance of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-19-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-126" role="math" style="width: 6.91em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 6.189em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1006.13em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-127"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-128" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">8.2</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-129" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">+</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-130" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic; padding-left: 0.243em;">j</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-131" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">195.0</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-132" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Â </span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-133" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î©</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-19">8.2+j195.0\ \Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> were simulated without modeling the plastic bottle cap in Momentum.</p><div class="section_2" id="sec2a"><h3>A. Measured Read Range of the Prototype RFID Tag</h3><p>Next, the read range of the prototype tag was measured to determine how well the antenna was matched with the input impedance of the Higgs-2 passive IC on the tag. To do this, an Alien Technology 9780 reader <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_2a">[8]</a> (with a maximum output power of 1 W) connected to a CP antenna with a gain of 6 dBi and the prototype tag on the plastic bottle were placed in an anechoic chamber. A max read range of 4.11 m was measured. This long read range indicates that a good match between the MOCSRR antenna and the input impedance of the Higgs-2 IC was obtained by attaching the tag to the plastic container. As a comparison, the read range of the larger meander-line antenna reported in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_2a">[10]</a> on a plastic container was 3.5 m. The read range of the prototype tag reported in this work is longer, and the overall size is 57.4% smaller than the prototype tag reported in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_2a">[10]</a>.</p><p>Also, the surface currents on the printed antenna were computed using Momentum and are shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4</a>. Furthermore, the far-field patterns in the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-20-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-134" role="math" style="width: 1.144em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1001.02em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-135"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-136" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">x</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-137" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.67em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-20">xz</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-21-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-138" role="math" style="width: 1.084em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.96em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-139"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-140" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">y<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-141" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; </p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig4"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/5423326/5608487/5608487-fig-4-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/5423326/5608487/5608487-fig-4-small.gif" alt="Figure 4" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 4. </b><fig><p>Simulated surface currents on the printed MOCSRR antenna.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5608487/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig5"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/5423326/5608487/5608487-fig-5-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/5423326/5608487/5608487-fig-5-small.gif" alt="Figure 5" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 5. </b><fig><p>Simulated far-field patterns in the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-22-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-142" role="math" style="width: 1.26em; Extracting the Equivalent Circuit of the MOCSRR Particle</h3><p>Next, to provide insight on the behavior of the MOCSRR dipole, the equivalent circuit of the MOCSRR particle shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2(b)</a> was extracted. The CPW structure in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2(c)</a> was used to extract the equivalent circuit of the MOCSRR particle (the same CPW structure was used in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_2b">[6]</a> to extract the equivalent circuit of the OCSRR particle). The dimensions of the MOCSRR particle in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2(c)</a> are the same as the dimensions of each particle used in the antenna design on the prototype tag (<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3</a>). First, the CPW structure in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2(c)</a> was modeled in Momentum <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_2b">[9]</a> (with the same substrate as the prototype RFID tag). The <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-24-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-150" role="math" style="width: 0.724em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.664em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.66em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-151"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-152" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-24">S</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-parameters for these simulations are shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 6</a>. When the MOCSRR particle resonates, the impedance on the CPW line caused by the particle approaches infinity. Therefore, when <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-25-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-153" role="math" style="width: 1.565em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.38em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-154"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-155"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-156" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-157"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-158"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-159" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">11</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-25">S_{11}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the lowest, the particles in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2(c)</a> are resonating. The simulated resonant frequency was <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-26-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-160" role="math" style="width: 6.249em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.589em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1005.53em 2.706em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-161"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-162"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.405em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-163" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">f<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-164"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-165"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-166" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-167" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">,</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-168" style="font-size: 70.7%; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-172" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">1.55</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; </p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig6"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/5423326/5608487/5608487-fig-6-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/5423326/5608487/5608487-fig-6-small.gif" alt="Figure 6" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 6. </b><fig><p><inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-27-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-173" role="math" style="width: 0.797em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.599em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.26em 1000.6em 2.384em -999.997em); top: -2.179em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-174"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-175" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.186em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.079em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.088em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-27">S</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-parameters of the MOCSRR particle.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5608487/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>Next, using a curve-fitting technique (similar to the approach used in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_2b">[6]</a>), the equivalent circuit of the MOCSRR particle was determined. The inductance and capacitance values in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2(b)</a> were computed to be <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-28-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-176" role="math" style="width: 6.009em; top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-177"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-178"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.225em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-180"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-181"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-182" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">e</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-183" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">q<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-184" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">,</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-185" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-186" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-187" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">3.75</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.397em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.203em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-28">L_{\rm eq,m}=3.75 </script></tex-math></inline-formula>nH and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-29-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-188" role="math" style="width: 5.468em; font-family: MathJax_Main;">e</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-195" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">q<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-196" style="font-size: 70.7%; Further discussion on the equivalent circuit extraction can be found in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_2b">[6]</a>. The <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-30-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-200" role="math" style="width: 0.724em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.664em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.66em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-201"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-202" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-30">S</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-parameters for the extracted equivalent circuit compare well to the simulations in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 6</a>. Next, the CPW structure in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2(c)</a> was manufactured, and the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-31-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-203" role="math" style="width: 0.724em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.664em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.66em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-204"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-205" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-31">S</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-parameters were measured using an Agilent Technologies 4.5-GHz E5071C ENA series network analyzer. The printed MOCSRR CPW structure is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7</a> (left side). The measured <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-32-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-206" role="math" style="width: 0.724em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.664em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.66em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-207"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-208" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-32">S</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-parameters are also shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 6</a>. The measured resonant frequency was <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-33-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-209" role="math" style="width: 6.73em; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-212" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">f<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-213"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-214"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-215" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-216" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">,</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-217" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">a</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-220" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">s</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-221" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-36">S</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-parameters compare very well. At 920 MHz, the MOCSRR particle has an impedance of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-37-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-240" role="math" style="width: 8.231em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 7.39em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1007.33em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-241"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-242"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.826em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-243" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-244"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-245"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-246" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-247" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">o</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-248" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">c</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-249" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">s</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-250" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">r</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-251" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">r</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-252" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-253" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic; padding-left: 0.303em;">j</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-254" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">30.8</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-255" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Â </span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-256" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î©</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-37">Z_{\rm mocsrr}=j30.8\ \Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. This shows that the inductance of the MOCSRR particle is dominant. Since the input impedance of an electrically small antenna is typically capacitive <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_2b">[4]</a>, this provides insight as to why the dipole on the prototype tag resonates at an overall dimension around <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-38-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-257" role="math" style="width: 2.526em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.285em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1002.28em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-258"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-259" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">0.1</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-260"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-261" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î»</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-262"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-263"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-264" style="font-size: 70.7%; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-38">0.1\lambda_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-39-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-265" role="math" style="width: 1.144em; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-269"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-270"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-271" style="font-size: 70.7%; Extracting the Equivalent Circuit of the OCSRR Particle</h3><p>Next, the equivalent circuit of the OCSRR particle in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8(a)</a> was extracted. This was done to compare the equivalent circuit of the OCSRR particle [<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8(b)</a>] introduced in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_2c">[6]</a> to the MOCSRR particle used in this letter. Using the CPW structure shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8(c)</a>, the same overall dimensions of MOCSRR particle used in the antenna design shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3(b)</a>, and the same substrate as the prototype RFID tag, an equivalent circuit of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-40-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-272" role="math" style="width: 5.168em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.628em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1004.57em 2.706em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-273"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-274"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.985em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-275" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-276"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-277"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-278" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">e</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-279" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">q<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-280" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">,</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-281" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">o</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-282" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.397em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.203em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-40">L_{\rm eq,o}=1.5 </script></tex-math></inline-formula>nH and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-41-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-284" role="math" style="width: 5.228em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.688em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.63em 2.706em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-285"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-286"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.045em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-287" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">C<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-288"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-289"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-290" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">e</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-291" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">q<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-292" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">,</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-293" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">o</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-294" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.397em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-41">C_{\rm eq,o}=3.2 </script></tex-math></inline-formula>pF was extracted using Momentum. The resonant frequency of the particle was <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-42-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-296" role="math" style="width: 5.949em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.348em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1005.29em 2.706em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-297"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-298"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.165em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-299" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">f<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-300"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-301"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-302" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">o</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-303" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">,</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-304" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-307" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-308" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">2.32</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.397em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-42">f_{\rm o,sim}=2.32 </script></tex-math></inline-formula> GHz. Finally, the CPW structure in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8(c)</a> was manufactured, and the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-43-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-309" role="math" style="width: 0.724em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.664em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.66em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-310"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-311" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-43">S</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-parameters were measured. The printed OCSRR CPW structure is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7</a> (right side). The measured resonant frequency was <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-44-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-312" role="math" style="width: 6.489em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.829em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1005.77em 2.706em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-313"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-314"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.646em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-315" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">f<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-316"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-317"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-318" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">o</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-319" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">,</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-320" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">a</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-323" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">s</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-324" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-325" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">2.28</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.397em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-44">f_{\rm o,meas}=2.28 </script></tex-math></inline-formula> GHz. The <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-45-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-326" role="math" style="width: 0.724em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.664em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.66em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-327"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-328" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-45">S</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-parameters compared well in all three cases (simulated, equivalent circuit, and measured). The results here show that the inductance of the MOCSRR particle is approximately twice the inductance of the OCSRR particle.

Using the CPW structure shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8(c)</a>, the dimensions of OCSRR particle defined in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_2c">[11]</a>, and the same substrate as the prototype RFID tag, an equivalent circuit of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-55-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-390" role="math" style="width: 6.61em; Characteristics of the MOCSRR Particle</h3><p>The equivalent circuit of the MOCSRR particle used on the prototype tag was computed next for various particle dimensions. First, the ring gap dimension <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-60-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-467" role="math" style="width: 0.544em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.483em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.48em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-468"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-469" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">g<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-60">g</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2(a)</a> was changed on an individual MOCSRR particle, and the equivalent circuit was extracted using Momentum. The results from these simulations are summarized in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">Table I</a>. Next, the ring gap was fixed at 0.31 mm, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-61-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-470" role="math" style="width: 0.483em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.423em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.42em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-471"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-472" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î´<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-61">\delta</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2(a)</a> was changed. Then, the equivalent circuit of the MOCSRR particle was determined for the various values of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-62-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-473" role="math" style="width: 0.483em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.423em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.42em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-474"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-475" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î´<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-62">\delta</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The results from these computations are also shown in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">Table I</a>. Finally, the input impedance of the antenna on the prototype RFID tag was computed for several ring gap dimensions <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-63-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-476" role="math" style="width: 0.544em; width: 0px; height: 2.186em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.079em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.004em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-68">t</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-69-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-494" role="math" style="width: 0.599em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.466em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.524em 1000.47em 2.583em -999.997em); top: -2.179em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-495"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-496" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">g<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.186em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.329em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.004em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-69">g</script></tex-math></inline-formula> were fixed for these computations).</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5608487/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full table" id="table1"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Table I </b>Equivalent Circuit for Various Particle Dimensions<div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/5423326/5608487/5608487-table-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/5423326/5608487/5608487-table-1-small.gif" alt="Table I" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div><p></p><p>The following useful comments can be made about the results in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">Table I</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Figs. 9</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig10" class="fulltext-link">10</a>.
</p><ol><li><p>The results in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">Table I</a> show how the resonant frequency of an individual particle can be increased by increasing the width of the ring gap <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-70-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-497" role="math" style="width: 0.544em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.483em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.48em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-498"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-499" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">g<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-70">g</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. In particular, the results in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">Table I</a> show how <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-71-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-500" role="math" style="width: 0.544em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.483em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.48em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-501"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-502" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">g<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-71">g</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is related to the equivalent capacitance of the MOCSRR particle. As <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-72-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-503" role="math" style="width: 0.544em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.483em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.48em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-504"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-505" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">g<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-72">g</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is reduced, the capacitance of the equivalent circuit is increased. This is expected because the distance between the inner meander ring and the surrounding conducting planes is being reduced, thus resulting in a larger capacitance.</p></li><li><p>The results in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">Table I</a> show the relation between the resonant frequency of the MOCSRR particle and the value of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-73-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-506" role="math" style="width: 0.483em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.423em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.42em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-507"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-508" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î´<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-73">\delta</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p></li><li><p>The results in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 9</a> show how both the real and imaginary parts of the input impedance of the prototype antenna are affected by various ring gap dimensions <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-74-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-509" role="math" style="width: 0.544em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.483em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.48em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-510"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-511" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">g<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-74">g</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p></li><li><p>The results in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig10" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 10</a> are particularly useful. These results show how the input impedance of the antenna is related to the values of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-75-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-512" role="math" style="width: 0.483em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.423em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.42em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-513"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-514" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î´<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-75">\delta</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. As the values of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-76-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-515" role="math" style="width: 0.483em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.423em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.42em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-516"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-517" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î´<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-76">\delta</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are changed, the real part of the input impedance of the antenna at 920 MHz can be modified to match the input impedance of the IC on the tag. This is very useful for a designer because the imaginary part of the input impedance of the antenna tends to change much less for various values of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-77-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-518" role="math" style="width: 0.483em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.423em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.42em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-519"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-520" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î´<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-77">\delta</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. This is interesting because many geometric changes to an antenna tend to effect both the real and imaginary parts of the input impedance of an antenna <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_2d">[10]</a>.</p></li></ol><p></p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Conclusion</h2></div><p>A new printed dipole design on a passive UHF RFID tag that uses series-connected meander open complementary split ring (MOCSRR) resonator particles has been presented. The equivalent circuit of various MOCSRR particles were extracted and compared to the equivalent circuit of published OCSRR particles. The relation between the equivalent circuit and the dimensions of the MOCSRR particle is also summarized. Furthermore, the input impedance of the antenna on the prototype RFID tag was computed for various MOCSRR particle dimensions.</p></div>
</div></div>

<script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

		}
	}
});

</script>
